One of Swift's earliest musical memories is listening to American opera singer and her maternal grandmother, [[Marjorie Finlay]], sing in church.<ref name=":5" /> As a child, she enjoyed [[The Walt Disney Company|Disney]] film soundtracks: "My parents noticed that, once I had run out of words, I would just make up my own".<ref name="theaustralian1">{{Cite news|url=http://www.theaustralian.com.au/arts/swift-rise-of-the-anti-diva/story-e6frg8n6-1111119032411|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141224030802/http://www.theaustralian.com.au/arts/swift-rise-of-the-anti-diva/story-e6frg8n6-1111119032411|archive-date=December 24, 2014|title=Swift rise of the anti-diva|first=Dan|last=Cairns|newspaper=[[The Australian]]|date=March 5, 2009|access-date=July 2, 2012}}</ref> Swift has said she owes her confidence to her mother, who helped her prepare for class presentations as a child.<ref>{{cite web|last=Bream|first=Jon|url=http://www.startribune.com/omg-taylor-s-senior-year/12149446/?elr=KArks%3ADCiU1PciUiD3aPc%3A_Yyc%3AaUoaEYY_1Pc_bDaEP7U|title=Music: OMG! Taylor's senior year|work=[[Star Tribune]]|date=December 7, 2007|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150712083112/http://www.startribune.com/omg-taylor-s-senior-year/12149446/?elr=KArks%3ADCiU1PciUiD3aPc%3A_Yyc%3AaUoaEYY_1Pc_bDaEP7U|archive-date=July 12, 2015}}</ref> She also attributes her "fascination with writing and storytelling" to her mother.<ref name="sessionsinterview" /> Swift was drawn to the storytelling aspect of country music,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=4649|title=Swift starts world tour in Asia, pushes "Speak Now' in NY|date=October 23, 2007|website=[[Country Standard Time]]|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121113072555/http://www.countrystandardtime.com/news/newsitem.asp?xid=4649|archive-date=November 13, 2012}}</ref> and was introduced to the genre listening to "the great female country artists of the '90s"—Shania Twain, Faith Hill, and the Dixie Chicks."<ref name="CMT 2007-11-12">{{cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1574118/20-questions-with-taylor-swift/|title=News : 20 Questions With Taylor Swift|date=November 12, 2007|publisher=[[Country Music Television|CMT]]|access-date=April 18, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20141117085801/http://www.cmt.com/news/1574118/20-questions-with-taylor-swift/|archive-date=November 17, 2014}}</ref><ref name="USAWEEKEND1">{{Cite news|first=Dennis|last=McCafferty|title=Taylor's Swift rise|url=http://159.54.226.237/08_issues/080413/080413taylor-swift.html|date=April 13, 2008|work=[[USA Weekend]]|access-date=April 17, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121114113840/http://159.54.226.237/08_issues/080413/080413taylor-swift.html|archive-date=November 14, 2012}}</ref> Twain, both as a songwriter and performer, was her biggest musical influence.<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://content.time.com/time/magazine/article/0,9171,1893502-1,00.html|title=Interview with Taylor Swift|work=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|date=April 23, 2009|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131023051246/http://content.time.com/time/magazine/article/0%2C9171%2C1893502-1%2C00.html|archive-date=October 23, 2013}}</ref> Hill was Swift's childhood role model: "Everything she said, did, wore, I tried to copy it".<ref>{{Cite news|title=Taylor Swift Style: Singer Won't Take Her Clothes Off, Wants People To Focus On Music|url=http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/10/23/taylor-swift-style-wont-take-her-clothes-off_n_2006776.html|access-date=January 4, 2015|work=[[HuffPost]]|date=October 23, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150104081258/http://www.huffingtonpost.com/2012/10/23/taylor-swift-style-wont-take-her-clothes-off_n_2006776.html|archive-date=January 4, 2015}}</ref> She admired the Dixie Chicks' defiant attitude and their ability to play their own instruments.<ref name="autogenerated2">{{cite web|url=http://www.instyle.co.uk/celebrity/news/instyle-meets-country-singing-sensation-taylor-swift|title=InStyle meets country singing sensation Taylor Swift|work=[[InStyle UK]]|date=October 26, 2010|access-date=May 29, 2012|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130527153326/http://www.instyle.co.uk/celebrity/news/instyle-meets-country-singing-sensation-taylor-swift|archive-date=May 27, 2013}}</ref> "[[Kiss Me (Sixpence None the Richer song)|Kiss Me]]" by [[Sixpence None the Richer]] was the first song Swift learned to play on the guitar.<ref>{{cite web|author=The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon|date=October 4, 2019|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=hQH6bv946T4&t=215s| archive-url=https://ghostarchive.org/varchive/youtube/20211029/hQH6bv946T4|  url-status=live | archive-date=2021-10-29|title=Name That Song Challenge with Taylor Swift (timestamp: 3:35)|website=YouTube|access-date=May 24, 2021}}{{cbignore}}</ref> Swift also explored the music of older country stars such as [[Patsy Cline]], [[Loretta Lynn]],  [[Tammy Wynette]], and [[Dolly Parton]],<ref name="Rolling Stone 2008-12-08" /> the latter of whom she believes is "an amazing example to every female songwriter out there",<ref name="billboard2">{{cite web|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/464865/taylor-swift-billboards-woman-of-the-year|title=Taylor Swift: Billboard's Woman of the Year|last=Roland|first=Tom|date=December 2, 2011|work=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130203232452/http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/464865/taylor-swift-billboards-woman-of-the-year|archive-date=February 3, 2013}}</ref> and [[alt-country]] artists like [[Patty Griffin]]<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.oprah.com/entertainment/Taylor-Swifts-Favorite-Music|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160116064914/http://www.oprah.com/entertainment/Taylor-Swifts-Favorite-Music|archive-date=January 16, 2016|title=Taylor Swift's Favorite Music|work=[[The Oprah Winfrey Show]]|access-date=October 23, 2012}}</ref> and [[Lori McKenna]].<ref name="widdicombe1" /> She has also cited [[Keith Urban]]'s musical style as an influence.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Reid|first=Poppy|date=November 2, 2021|title=The Curious Case of Keith Urban|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-country/keith-urban-australia-sobriety-interview-1250442/|access-date=November 3, 2021|magazine=Rolling Stone|language=en-US}}</ref>

Swift has also been influenced by various pop and rock artists. She lists [[Paul McCartney]], [[Bruce Springsteen]], [[Bryan Adams]],<ref>{{Cite magazine|date=August 5, 2018|title=Taylor Swift Surprises Toronto Crowd With Bryan Adams 'Summer of '69' Duet: Watch|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/8468681/taylor-swift-bryan-adams-summer-of-69-live-toronto|access-date=August 30, 2020|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> [[Emmylou Harris]], [[Kris Kristofferson]], and [[Carly Simon]] as her career role models. Discussing McCartney and Harris, Swift has said, "They've taken chances, but they've also been the same artist for their entire careers".<ref name="widdicombe1" /><ref name="usatoday1">{{Cite news|last=Mansfield|first=Brian|url=http://usatoday30.usatoday.com/life/music/news/2010-10-22-taylorswift22_CV_N.htm|title=Taylor Swift learns to 'Speak Now,' reveal her maturity|work=[[USA Today]]|date=October 23, 2010|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121104201421/http://usatoday30.usatoday.com/life/music/news/2010-10-22-taylorswift22_CV_N.htm|archive-date=November 4, 2012}}</ref> McCartney, both as a [[The Beatles|Beatle]] and a solo artist, makes Swift feel "as if I've been let into his heart and his mind&nbsp;[...] He's out there continuing to make his fans so happy. Any musician could only dream of a legacy like that."<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.people.com/people/archive/article/0,,20567076,00.html|title=Rolling in the Trophies? – Adele|work=[[People (magazine)|People]]|date=February 6, 2012|access-date=July 3, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120601020156/http://www.people.com/people/archive/article/0%2C%2C20567076%2C00.html|archive-date=June 1, 2012}}</ref> She likes Springsteen for being "so musically relevant after such a long period of time".<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://www.ew.com/ew/article/0,,20434320_2,00.html|title=Taylor Swift Goes Record Shopping with EW|work=[[Entertainment Weekly]]|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130502202650/http://www.ew.com/ew/article/0%2C%2C20434320_2%2C00.html|archive-date=May 2, 2013}}</ref> She aspires to be like Harris as she grows older because of prioritizing music over fame.<ref>{{cite web|url=http://www.channelguidemag.com/tv-news/2008/11/02/our-interview-with-taylor-swift/|title=Our Interview with Taylor Swift|publisher=Channelguidemagblog.com|type=Blog|date=November 2, 2008|access-date=February 25, 2013|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160116064918/http://www.channelguidemag.com/tv-news/2008/11/02/our-interview-with-taylor-swift/|archive-date=January 16, 2016}}</ref> Swift says of Kristofferson that he "shines in songwriting",<ref name="single life">{{Cite news|last=Van Meter|first=Jonathan|url=http://www.vogue.com/865383/taylor-swift-the-single-life/#1|title=Taylor Swift: The Single Life|work=[[Vogue (magazine)|Vogue]]|access-date=July 3, 2012|date=January 17, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140908124308/http://www.vogue.com/865383/taylor-swift-the-single-life/#1|archive-date=September 8, 2014}}</ref> and admires Simon for being "an emotional" but "a strong person".<ref name=":3">{{Cite news|url=http://www.news.com.au/entertainment/music/taylor-swift-is-happy-to-be-your-break-up-musician/story-e6frfn09-1226644234716|title=Taylor Swift is happy to be your break-up musician|last=Adams|first=Cameron|date=May 16, 2013|publisher=[[News.com.au]]|access-date=June 10, 2013|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130519111037/http://www.news.com.au/entertainment/music/taylor-swift-is-happy-to-be-your-break-up-musician/story-e6frfn09-1226644234716|archive-date=May 19, 2013}}</ref> Her synth-pop album ''1989'' was influenced by some of her favorite 1980s pop acts, including [[Peter Gabriel]], [[Annie Lennox]], [[Phil Collins]] and [[Madonna]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.npr.org/2014/10/31/359827368/anything-that-connects-a-conversation-with-taylor-swift|title='Anything That Connects': A Conversation With Taylor Swift|website=[[NPR Music]]|date=October 31, 2014|access-date=October 26, 2019}}</ref><ref name="likeaprayer">{{cite web|first=Josh|last=Eells|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/features/taylor-swift-1989-cover-story-20140908|title=The Reinvention of Taylor Swift|date=September 8, 2014|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=June 8, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160604183110/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/features/taylor-swift-1989-cover-story-20140908|archive-date=June 4, 2016}}</ref> As a songwriter, Swift was influenced by [[Joni Mitchell]] for her autobiographical lyrics conveying the deepest emotions: "She wrote it about her deepest pains and most haunting demons ... I think [''[[Blue (Joni Mitchell album)|Blue]]''] is my favorite because it explores somebody's soul so deeply".<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/joni-mitchell-15-great-artists-influenced-by-the-blue-singer-168972/taylor-swift-30-154837/|title=Joni Mitchell: 15 Great Artists Influenced by the 'Blue' Singer|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=June 22, 2016|access-date=December 26, 2020}}</ref>

=== Musical styles ===
Swift's discography spans country, pop, [[Folk music|folk]], and [[Alternative rock|alternative]] genres.<ref name=":14" /><ref>{{Cite web |title=Taylor Swift |url=https://www.officialcharts.com/artist/5387/taylor-swift/ |access-date=November 3, 2021 |website=[[Official Charts Company]]}}</ref> Her first three studio albums ''Taylor Swift'', ''Fearless'' and ''Speak Now'' are categorized as country;<ref name=":18">{{Cite web|last=Dowd|first=Rachael|date=July 24, 2021|title=Taylor Swift's 'folklore' is her first album to be classified as alternative|url=https://www.altpress.com/news/taylor-swift-folklore-alternative-classification/|access-date=November 3, 2021|website=[[Alternative Press (magazine)|Alternative Press]]|language=en-US}}</ref> her eclectic fourth studio album, ''Red'', is dubbed both country and pop;<ref name=":17" /> her next three albums ''1989'', ''Reputation'' and ''Lover'' are labeled pop; and ''Folklore'' and ''Evermore'' are considered alternative.<ref name=":18" /> Music critics have described her songs as [[synth-pop]],<ref name="synth pop">{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/all-129-of-taylor-swifts-songs-ranked-201800/|title=All 129 of Taylor Swift's Songs, Ranked|last=Sheffield|first=Rob|date=September 21, 2017|website=[[Rolling Stone (magazine)|Rolling Stone]]|access-date=October 13, 2019}}</ref> [[country pop]],<ref>{{cite news|last1=Carson|first1=Sarah|title=The Story of Taylor Swift: 10 years at the top in her own lyrics|url=https://www.telegraph.co.uk/music/artists/taylor-swifts-10-years-at-the-top-in-her-own-lyrics/|newspaper=[[The Daily Telegraph]]|date=October 24, 2016|access-date=September 14, 2019}}</ref> [[Rock music|rock]],<ref name="synth pop" /> [[electropop]],<ref name=":15">{{Cite news|last=Tucker|first=Ken|date=November 13, 2017|title=Taylor Swift Pushes Further Into Electro-Pop With ''Reputation''|work=[[NPR]]|url=https://www.npr.org/2017/11/13/563738577/taylor-swift-pushes-further-into-electro-pop-with-reputation|access-date=October 26, 2021}}</ref> and [[Indie pop|indie]], amongst others;<ref>{{Cite web|date=December 11, 2020|title=Taylor Swift – ''Evermore'': the NME review|url=https://www.nme.com/reviews/taylor-swift-evermore-review-2835933|access-date=December 12, 2020|website=NME}}</ref> some songs, especially those on ''Reputation'', incorporate elements of R&B, [[electronic dance music|EDM]], hip hop, and [[trap music|trap]].<ref name=":19">{{Cite web|last=da Silva|first=Michelle|date=November 13, 2017|title=Taylor Swift has changed for the worse on Reputation|url=https://nowtoronto.com/music/album-reviews/taylor-swift-bad-reputation|access-date=July 27, 2020|website=[[Now (newspaper)|Now]]}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Schonfeld|first=Zach|date=November 14, 2017|title=Taylor Swift's 'Reputation': A Track-by-Track Review, from '...Ready for It?' to 'New Year's Day'|url=https://www.newsweek.com/taylor-swift-reputation-album-review-gorgeous-ready-708853|access-date=July 27, 2020|website=Newsweek}}</ref> The music instruments Swift plays include the piano, [[banjo]], [[ukulele]] and various types of guitar.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Brown|first=Lisa|date=October 30, 2016|title=Taylor Swift's 7 Best Songs On Piano|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/7557765/taylor-swifts-best-songspiano|access-date=January 21, 2021|magazine=Billboard}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Preston|first=Stefan|date=October 5, 2019|title=Taylor Swift Proves She's a Musical Genius But Doesn't Recognize Her Own Hit Song|url=https://www.cheatsheet.com/entertainment/taylor-swift-proves-shes-a-musical-genius-but-doesnt-recognize-her-own-hit-song.html/|access-date=January 21, 2021|website=Showbiz CheatSheet}}</ref> Swift described herself as a country artist until the release of ''1989'', which she characterized as her first "sonically cohesive pop album".<ref name="tennessean.com">{{cite web|url=http://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/music/peter-cooper/2014/10/26/taylor-swift-reaches-turning-point/17871775/|title=Taylor Swift reaches a turning point with '1989'|last=Cooper|first=Peter|date=October 26, 2014|archive-url=https://www.webcitation.org/6klhMwBEm?url=http://www.tennessean.com/story/entertainment/music/peter-cooper/2014/10/26/taylor-swift-reaches-turning-point/17871775/|archive-date=September 24, 2016|work=[[The Tennessean]]|access-date=April 11, 2015|url-status=dead}}</ref>

{{Quote|text=If there's one thing that Swift has proven throughout her career, it's that she refuses to be put in a box. Her ever-evolving sound took her from country darling to pop phenom to folk's newest raconteur—a transition that, on paper, seems arduous [...] Her wordcraft is some of the most alluring of her generation, and that's never been lost on her music, regardless of the genre she's exploring.|author=[[The Recording Academy]] on Swift<ref>{{cite web|last=Weatherby|first=Taylor|date=March 10, 2021|title=Taylor Swift's Road To 'Folklore'|url=https://www.grammy.com/grammys/news/taylor-swift-folklore-2021-grammys|access-date=November 24, 2021|website=[[The Recording Academy|Grammy.com]]}}</ref>|source=}}

''Rolling Stone'' wrote, "[Swift] might get played on the country station, but she's one of the few genuine rock stars we've got these days."<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/lists/women-who-rock-the-50-greatest-albums-of-all-time-20120622/taylor-swift-speak-now-19691231|title=Women Who Rock: The 50 Greatest Albums of All Time: Taylor Swift, 'Speak Now'|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120712013447/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/lists/women-who-rock-the-50-greatest-albums-of-all-time-20120622/taylor-swift-speak-now-19691231|archive-date=July 12, 2012|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=July 30, 2012|date=June 22, 2012}}</ref> According to ''The New York Times'', "There isn't much in Ms. Swift's music to indicate country—a few banjo strums, a pair of cowboy boots worn onstage, a bedazzled guitar—but there's something in her winsome, vulnerable delivery that's unique to Nashville."<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2011/07/22/arts/music/pop-and-rock-listings-july-22-28.html|title=Pop and Rock Listings July 22 – 28|date=July 21, 2011|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=July 12, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120128232427/http://www.nytimes.com/2011/07/22/arts/music/pop-and-rock-listings-july-22-28.html|archive-date=January 28, 2012}}</ref> ''[[The Guardian]]'' wrote that Swift "cranks melodies out with the pitiless efficiency of a Scandinavian pop factory."<ref name="guardian1">{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2009/mar/06/taylor-swift-fearless-album-review|title=Taylor Swift: Fearless|last=Petridis|first=Alexis|date=March 6, 2009|work=[[The Guardian]]|location=London|access-date=June 24, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131016160252/http://www.theguardian.com/music/2009/mar/06/taylor-swift-fearless-album-review|archive-date=October 16, 2013}}</ref> [[Consequence (publication)|''Consequence'']] pinpointed her "capacity to continually reinvent while remaining herself",<ref name=":21" /> while ''[[Time (magazine)|Time]]'' dubbed Swift a "musical chameleon" for the constantly evolving sound of her discography.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Bruner|first=Raisa|date=July 24, 2020|title=Let's Break Down Taylor Swift's Tender New Album Folklore|url=https://time.com/5871159/taylor-swift-folklore-explained/|access-date=November 10, 2021|magazine=Time|language=en}}</ref> ''[[Clash (magazine)|Clash]]'' said her career "has always been one of transcendence and covert boundary-pushing", reaching a point at which "Taylor Swift is just Taylor Swift", not defined by any genre.<ref name=":23">{{Cite web|last=Harbron|first=Lucy|date=November 11, 2021|title=Why Taylor Swift's 'Red' Is Her Turning Point|url=https://www.clashmusic.com/features/why-taylor-swifts-red-is-her-turning-point|access-date=November 12, 2021|website=Clash|language=en}}</ref>

=== Voice ===
Swift possesses a [[mezzo-soprano]] [[Voice type|vocal range]].<ref name="Singing">{{Cite book|title=An Idiots Guide: Singing Second Edition |last=Fulford |first= Phyllis|year= 2014|publisher= Penguin Publishing|isbn= 978-1-61564-622-7|page= 192|url= https://books.google.com/books?id=XxU-BAAAQBAJ&q=taylor+swift+AND+mezzo&pg=PA192}}</ref> Her singing voice is "sweet but soft" according to Sophie Schillaci of ''[[The Hollywood Reporter]]''.<ref name="schillaci1">{{Cite news|url=http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/review/taylor-swift-at-staples-center-227968|title=Taylor Swift at Staples Center: Concert Review|last=Schillaci|first=Sophie A.|date=August 25, 2011|work=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|access-date=August 2, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160304025206/http://www.hollywoodreporter.com/review/taylor-swift-at-staples-center-227968|archive-date=March 4, 2016}}</ref> ''[[Pitchfork (website)|Pitchfork]]''<nowiki/>'s Sam Sodomsky called it "versatile and expressive".<ref>{{Cite web|last=Sodomsky|first=Sam|date=December 15, 2020|title=Taylor Swift: evermore Review|url=https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/taylor-swift-evermore/|access-date=April 9, 2021|website=Pitchfork}}</ref> [[Music theory]] professor Alyssa Barna described the [[timbre]] of Swift's upper [[Register (music)|register]] as "breathy and bright", and her lower register "full and dark".<ref>{{Cite web|last=Barna|first=Alyssa|date=December 16, 2020|title=These are the musicological reasons Taylor Swift's new album sounds dull|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/outlook/2020/12/16/taylor-swift-musicology-evermore-boring/|url-access=subscription|access-date=November 3, 2021|website=[[The Washington Post]]}}</ref> The ''Los Angeles Times'' identified Swift's "defining" vocal gesture in studio recordings as "the line that slides down like a contented sigh or up like a raised eyebrow, giving her beloved girl-time hits their air of easy intimacy."<ref name="LAT">{{Cite news|url=http://latimesblogs.latimes.com/music_blog/2010/10/album-review-taylor-swifts-speak-now.html|title=Album review: Taylor Swift's 'Speak Now'|last=Powers|first=Ann|date=October 25, 2010|work=[[Los Angeles Times]]|type=Blog|access-date=October 25, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101028003032/http://latimesblogs.latimes.com/music_blog/2010/10/album-review-taylor-swifts-speak-now.html|archive-date=October 28, 2010}}</ref> In 2010, a writer from ''[[The Tennessean]]'' conceded that Swift was "not the best technical singer", but described her as the "best communicator that we've got".<ref>{{cite web|url=http://blogs.tennessean.com/tunein/2010/02/01/taylor-swift-has-mixed-reviews-from-grammy-night/|title=Taylor Swift gets mixed reviews at Grammys|date=February 1, 2010|type=Blog|archive-url=https://archive.today/20150713203631/http://blogs.tennessean.com/tunein/2010/02/01/taylor-swift-has-mixed-reviews-from-grammy-night/|archive-date=July 13, 2015|work=[[The Tennessean]]|access-date=June 24, 2012}}</ref> Her vocal ability is something that has often concerned Swift in her early career, and she has "put a lot of work" into improving it.<ref name="Up for Discussion">{{cite web|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/news/953737/taylor-swift-the-billboard-cover-story|title=Taylor Swift: The Billboard Cover Story|last=Roland|first=Tom|date=October 15, 2010|work=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=July 3, 2012|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20101018200303/http://www.billboard.com/features/taylor-swift-the-billboard-cover-story-1004121338.story|archive-date=October 18, 2010|url-status=dead}}</ref> She said she only feels nervous performing live "if I'm not sure what the audience thinks of me, like at award shows".<ref>{{cite magazine|date=June 27, 2011|title=Taylor Swift on Performing, Her Friends, and Favorite Songs|url=https://www.teenvogue.com/gallery/taylor-swift-teen-vogue-photos|magazine=[[Teen Vogue]]|access-date=March 5, 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20180705024528/https://www.teenvogue.com/gallery/taylor-swift-teen-vogue-photos|archive-date=July 5, 2018}}</ref>

In 2011, ''Rolling Stone'' wrote: "Swift's voice is unaffected enough to mask how masterful she has become as a singer; she lowers her voice for the payoff lines in the classic mode of a shy girl trying to talk tough."<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/albumreviews/speak-now-20101026|title=Speak Now|last=Sheffield|first=Rob|date=October 26, 2010|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=June 15, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://www.webcitation.org/5vpXbTcTi?url=http://www.rollingstone.com/music/albumreviews/speak-now-20101026|archive-date=January 18, 2011}}</ref> ''[[The Village Voice]]'' wrote that her phrasing was previously "bland and muddled, but that's changed. She can still sound strained and thin, and often strays into a pitch that drives some people crazy; but she's learned how to make words sound like what they mean."<ref name="Voice">{{cite web|url=http://www.villagevoice.com/music/the-iceberg-songs-of-taylor-swift-6429071|title=The Iceberg Songs of Taylor Swift|last=Weber|first=Theon|date=November 3, 2010|work=[[The Village Voice]]|access-date=November 3, 2010|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151104105408/http://www.villagevoice.com/music/the-iceberg-songs-of-taylor-swift-6429071|archive-date=November 4, 2015}}</ref> In 2014, [[NPR Music]] described her singing as personal and conversational thanks to her "exceptional gift for inflection", but also suffered from a "wobbly pitch and tight, nasal delivery".<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.npr.org/sections/therecord/2014/10/30/360129727/the-many-new-voices-of-taylor-swift|title=The Many New Voices Of Taylor Swift|last=Powers|first=Ann|website=[[NPR Music]]|date=October 30, 2014|access-date=October 26, 2019}}</ref> ''The Hollywood Reporter'' wrote that her live vocals were "fine", but did not match those of her peers.<ref name="schillaci1" /> Swift was praised for refusing to correct her pitch with [[Auto-Tune]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=http://archive.boston.com/ae/music/articles/2010/10/24/taylor_swift_comes_into_her_own_with_speak_now/|title=Swift's ascent continues with arrival of new album|last=Reed|first=James|date=October 24, 2010|work=[[Boston Globe]]|access-date=August 23, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160927023835/http://archive.boston.com/ae/music/articles/2010/10/24/taylor_swift_comes_into_her_own_with_speak_now/|archive-date=September 27, 2016}}</ref>

In 2020, ''[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]'' critic Andrew Barker said Swift has developed "remarkable" control over her vocals, never allowing a "flourish or a tricky run to compromise the clarity of a lyric", while doing "wonders within her register" and "exploring its further reaches".<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Barker|first=Andrew|date=November 27, 2020|title='Folklore: The Long Pond Studio Sessions' Review|url=https://variety.com/2020/film/reviews/folklore-the-long-pond-studio-sessions-film-review-taylor-swift-1234840985/|access-date=May 31, 2021|magazine=Variety}}</ref> Reviewing Swift's 2021 re-recording of ''Fearless'', ''[[The New York Times]]'' critic Lindsay Zoladz wrote that her voice became stronger, more controlled, and deeper over time, discarding the nasal tone of her early vocals.<ref name=":02">{{cite news|last=Zoladz|first=Lindsay|date=April 9, 2021|title=Taylor Swift Remade 'Fearless' as 'Taylor's Version.' Let's Discuss.|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/arts/music/taylor-swift-fearless-taylors-version.html|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210409224903/https://www.nytimes.com/2021/04/09/arts/music/taylor-swift-fearless-taylors-version.html|archive-date=April 9, 2021|access-date=April 21, 2021|newspaper=[[The New York Times]]}}</ref> Lucy Harbron of ''[[Clash (magazine)|Clash]]'' opined that Swift's vocals have evolved "into her own unique blend of country, pop and indie".<ref name="Clash review">{{Cite magazine|last=Harbron|first=Lucy|date=April 9, 2021|title=Taylor Swift – Fearless (Taylor's Version)|url=https://www.clashmusic.com/reviews/taylor-swift-fearless-taylors-version|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210409075926/https://www.clashmusic.com/reviews/taylor-swift-fearless-taylors-version|archive-date=April 9, 2021|access-date=April 21, 2021|magazine=[[Clash (magazine)|Clash]]}}</ref>

=== Songwriting ===
{{Blockquote|text=I love songwriting so much because there's an element to it that is still really mysterious—like I think any songwriter will tell you, when you get an idea you're not quite sure where it floated down from, but if you can grab onto that idea and turn it into something, a piece of music, that's where craftsmanship comes in; that’s where you have the opportunity to learn and to nurture that craft.|author=Swift on the art of songwriting|source=''[[Variety (magazine)|Variety]]''<ref>{{Cite web |last=Aswad |first=Jem |title=Read Taylor Swift's Speech on the 'Magical, Mystical' Art of Songwriting When Accepting NMPA Icon Award |url=https://variety.com/2021/music/news/taylor-swift-speech-nmpa-songwriter-icon-award-1234993003/ |access-date=October 31, 2021 |website=Variety |date=June 9, 2021}}</ref>}}

Swift has been referred to as one of the greatest songwriters of all time and the best of her generation by various publications and organizations.<ref>{{Cite web|date=August 22, 2019|title=Taylor Swift's songwriting: how the star's music has changed, for better or worse|url=https://www.cbc.ca/amp/1.5246984|access-date=November 10, 2021|website=[[CBC Music]]}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Alcala|first=Mark|date=April 12, 2019|title=Why Taylor Swift Is The Greatest Songwriter In Her Generation|url=https://www.latintimes.com/why-taylor-swift-greatest-songwriter-her-generation-437826|access-date=November 10, 2021|website=[[Latin Times]]|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Emily|first=Lee|date=November 5, 2021|title=Here Are Taylor Swift's Best Bridges On 'Red' Ranked|url=https://www.iheart.com/content/2021-11-05-here-are-taylor-swifts-best-bridges-on-red-ranked|access-date=2021-11-10|website=iHeartRadio|language=en}}</ref><ref name=":22" /> In a 2011 interview with ''[[The New Yorker]]'', Swift identified primarily as a songwriter: "I write songs, and my voice is just a way to get those lyrics across."<ref name="widdicombe1" /> Swift's personal experiences were a common inspiration for her early songs, which helped her navigate the complexities of life.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.wsj.com/articles/SB10001424052702304510704575562401576663866|title=Taylor Swift's Solo Act|last=Farley|first=Christopher John|date=October 22, 2010|newspaper=[[The Wall Street Journal]]|access-date=May 24, 2012|url-status=live|url-access=subscription|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150201211555/http://www.wsj.com/articles/SB10001424052702304510704575562401576663866|archive-date=February 1, 2015}}</ref><ref name="telltale">{{Cite news|last1=Jo Sales|first1=Nancy|last2=Diehl|first2=Jessica|date=April 2013|title=Taylor Swift's Telltale Heart|work=[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]|url=http://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2013/04/taylor-swift-cover-story|url-status=live|access-date=February 4, 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20170130205206/http://www.vanityfair.com/hollywood/2013/04/taylor-swift-cover-story|archive-date=January 30, 2017}}</ref> Her "diaristic" technique began with identifying an emotion, followed by a corresponding melody.<ref name="ZaneLowe">{{cite web|url=https://www.nme.com/news/music/taylor-swift-diaristic-songwriting-style-unsustainable-future-folklore-evermore-2837843|title=Taylor Swift says her diaristic songwriting style was 'unsustainable' for her future|work=[[NME]]|first=Rhian|last=Daly|date=December 13, 2020|access-date=February 17, 2021}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130614085411/https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/474541/taylor-swifts-red-the-billboard-cover-story|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/474541/taylor-swifts-red-the-billboard-cover-story|title=Taylor Swift's ''Red'': The Billboard Cover Story|first=Phil|last=Gallo|date=October 22, 2012|archive-date=June 14, 2013|work=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]}}</ref> On her first three studio albums, recurring themes were love, heartbreak, and insecurities, from an adolescent perspective.<ref name="nytimes1">{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2010/10/24/arts/music/24swift.html?pagewanted=all|title=Taylor Swift Is Angry, Darn It|last=Caramanica|first=Jon|date=October 20, 2010|work=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=July 2, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120911131428/http://www.nytimes.com/2010/10/24/arts/music/24swift.html?pagewanted=all|archive-date=September 11, 2012}}</ref><ref name=":16">{{Cite news|last=Kelly|first=James|url=http://www.accessatlanta.com/news/entertainment/music/taylor-swift-writing-her-own-songs-and-rules/nQy5n/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20140908123045/http://www.accessatlanta.com/news/entertainment/music/taylor-swift-writing-her-own-songs-and-rules/nQy5n/|archive-date=September 8, 2014|title=Taylor Swift writing her own songs and rules|work=[[The Atlanta Journal-Constitution]]|date=August 26, 2009|access-date=July 30, 2012}}</ref> She delved into the tumult of toxic relationships on ''Red'',<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/8030142/taylor-swift-red-best-album/|title=Why Taylor Swift's ''Red'' Is Her Best Album|date=November 8, 2017|work=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=December 27, 2020|first=Sam|last=Lansky}}</ref> and embraced nostalgia and positivity after failed relationships on ''1989''.<ref>{{cite news|first=Melissa|last=Block|title='Anything That Connects': A Conversation With Taylor Swift|url=https://www.npr.org/2014/10/31/359827368/anything-that-connects-a-conversation-with-taylor-swift|work=[[NPR Music]]|access-date=January 30, 2015|format=Audio upload and transcript|date=October 31, 2014|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20150206065548/http://www.npr.org/2014/10/31/359827368/anything-that-connects-a-conversation-with-taylor-swift|archive-date=February 6, 2015|url-status=live}}</ref> ''Reputation'' was inspired by Swift's celebrity,<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/taylor-swift-moments-that-couldnt-fit-in-our-cover-story-890700/|title=9 Taylor Swift Moments That Didn't Fit in Our Cover Story|last=Hiatt|first=Brian|date=September 30, 2019|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|access-date=December 9, 2019|archive-date=October 1, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20191001144210/https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/taylor-swift-moments-that-couldnt-fit-in-our-cover-story-890700/|url-status=live}}</ref> and ''Lover'' detailed her realization of the "full spectrum of love".<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://onairwithryan.iheart.com/featured/ryan-seacrest/content/2019-08-27-taylor-swift-talks-newfound-freedom-lover-tour-plans-and-so-much-more/|title=Taylor Swift Talks Newfound 'Freedom,' 'Lover' Tour Plans and So Much More|website=[[On Air with Ryan Seacrest]]|date=August 27, 2019|access-date=March 22, 2020}}</ref> Besides romance, other themes in Swift's music include parent-child relationships, friendships,<ref>{{cite web|url=http://lasvegasweekly.com/ae/music/2009/dec/30/microwaving-tragedy-marriage-romance-and-romantici/|title=Microwaving a tragedy: The marriage of romance and romanticism in '00s pop|work=[[Las Vegas Weekly]]|date=December 30, 2009|last=Yuan|first=Jada|access-date=August 17, 2012|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131221052022/http://www.lasvegasweekly.com/ae/music/2009/dec/30/microwaving-tragedy-marriage-romance-and-romantici/|archive-date=December 21, 2013}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Rotman|first=Natalie|url=http://readingeagle.com/article.aspx?id=154886|title=Colbie Caillat has 'Breakthrough' with sophomore CD|work=[[Reading Eagle]]|date=January 9, 2009|access-date=August 17, 2012|url-status=dead|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20131221001640/http://www2.readingeagle.com/article.aspx?id=154886|archive-date=December 21, 2013}}</ref> alienation, and self-awareness.<ref name="sessionsinterview">{{cite web|url=http://music.aol.com/sessions/taylor-swift-change-sessions/|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121009010116/http://music.aol.com/sessions/taylor-swift-change-sessions/|archive-date=October 9, 2012|title=Taylor Swift Sessions Interview|first=Melinda|last=Newman|date=December 19, 2008|work=[[AOL]]|access-date=March 25, 2011}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|title=Taylor Swift's songwriting: how the star's music has changed, for better or worse|work=[[CBC News]]|url=https://www.cbc.ca/music/taylor-swift-s-songwriting-how-the-star-s-music-has-changed-for-better-or-worse-1.5246984|access-date=February 2, 2021}}</ref>

Swift's confessional narratives received critical praise.<ref name="widdicombe1" /><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nme.com/features/taylor-swift-power-fame-and-the-future-the-full-nme-cover-interview-549|title=Taylor Swift: Power, Fame And The Future&nbsp;– The Full ''NME'' Cover Interview|first=Dan|last=Stubbs|work=[[NME]]|date=October 9, 2015|access-date=February 17, 2021}}</ref> Music critics complimented Swift's songwriting for its vivid details and emotional engagement, which were uncommon among other pop artists.<ref name="iceberg">{{cite web|url=http://www.villagevoice.com/music/the-iceberg-songs-of-taylor-swift-6429071|title=The Iceberg Songs of Taylor Swift|last=Weber|first=Theon|date=November 3, 2010|work=[[The Village Voice]]|access-date=July 30, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151104105408/http://www.villagevoice.com/music/the-iceberg-songs-of-taylor-swift-6429071|archive-date=November 4, 2015}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Beck|first=Julia|date=October 27, 2014|title=Taylor Swift Is So Much More Fun Now That She's Jaded|work=[[The Atlantic]]|url=http://www.theatlantic.com/entertainment/archive/2014/10/1989-reviewed-taylor-swift-grows-up-goes-pop/381948/|access-date=October 30, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160927113413/http://www.theatlantic.com/entertainment/archive/2014/10/1989-reviewed-taylor-swift-grows-up-goes-pop/381948/|archive-date=September 27, 2016}}</ref> ''New York'' magazine argued that Swift was the first teenage artist who explicitly portrayed teenage experiences in her music.<ref name="nymag">{{cite web|url=http://nymag.com/arts/popmusic/features/68796/|title=Princess Crossover|work=[[New York (magazine)|New York]]|date=October 10, 2010|access-date=July 1, 2012|last=Willman|first=Chris|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20130727141326/http://nymag.com/arts/popmusic/features/68796/|archive-date=July 27, 2013}}</ref> ''Rolling Stone'' described Swift as "a songwriting savant with an intuitive gift for [[song structure|verse-chorus-bridge architecture]]".<ref name="rollingstone2">{{cite web|last=Rosen|first=Jody|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/albumreviews/fearless-20081113|title=Fearless|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=November 13, 2008|access-date=July 1, 2012|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20120815082027/http://www.rollingstone.com/music/albumreviews/fearless-20081113|archive-date=August 15, 2012}}</ref> Although reviews of Swift are generally positive, ''The New Yorker'' stated she was generally portrayed "more as a skilled technician than as a [[Bob Dylan|Dylanesque]] visionary".<ref name="widdicombe1" /> Because of her confessional narratives, [[Tabloid journalism|tabloid media]] often speculated and linked the subjects of the songs with ex-lovers of Swift, a practice which ''New York'' magazine considered "[[Sexism|sexist]], inasmuch as it's not asked of her male peers".<ref name="iceberg" /><ref>{{cite web|url=http://nymag.com/thecut/2012/11/stop-asking-taylor-swift-to-apologize.html|title=Stop Asking Taylor Swift to Apologize for Writing Songs About Ex-Boyfriends – The Cut|date=November 16, 2012|work=[[New York (magazine)|New York]]|access-date=February 25, 2013|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20121127200757/http://nymag.com/thecut/2012/11/stop-asking-taylor-swift-to-apologize.html|archive-date=November 27, 2012}}</ref> Aside from clues provided in album [[liner notes]], Swift avoided talking about song subjects specifically.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/18/magazine/the-many-insecurities-of-taylor-swift.html|title=The Many Insecurities of Taylor Swift|last=Dominus|first=Susan|date=November 16, 2012|work=[[The New York Times]]|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160617050939/http://www.nytimes.com/2012/11/18/magazine/the-many-insecurities-of-taylor-swift.html|archive-date=June 17, 2016}}</ref> In a 2013 interview with ''[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]'', Swift stated that the criticism on her songwriting—critics interpreted her persona as a "clingy, insane, desperate girlfriend in need of making you marry her and have kids with her"—was "a little sexist".<ref name="Zach Johnson">{{Cite magazine|url=http://www.vanityfair.com/culture/2013/03/taylor-swift-fights-back-tina-fey-amy-poehler|title=Cover Preview: Taylor Swift Fights Back About Her Love Life, the Hyannis Port House—and Has Words for Tina Fey and Amy Poehler|magazine=[[Vanity Fair (magazine)|Vanity Fair]]|date=March 5, 2013|access-date=August 3, 2016|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160808192844/http://www.vanityfair.com/culture/2013/03/taylor-swift-fights-back-tina-fey-amy-poehler|archive-date=August 8, 2016}}</ref>

On her 2020 albums ''Folklore'' and ''Evermore'', Swift was inspired by [[escapism]] and [[romanticism]] to explore fictional narratives.<ref name="musicians on musicians" /> Without referencing her personal life, she imposed her emotions onto imagined characters and story arcs, which liberated her from the mental stress caused by tabloid attention and suggested new paths for her artistry.<ref name="ZaneLowe" /> In a feature for ''Rolling Stone'', Swift explained that she welcomed the new songwriting direction after she stopped worrying about commercial success: "I always thought, 'That'll never track on [[Contemporary hit radio|pop radio]],' but when I was making ''Folklore'', I thought, 'If you take away all the parameters, what do you make?"<ref name="musicians on musicians">{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-features/paul-mccartney-taylor-swift-musicians-on-musicians-1089058/|title=Musicians on Musicians: Paul McCartney and Taylor Swift|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|first=Patrick|last=Doyle|date=November 13, 2020|access-date=February 7, 2021}}</ref> With the release of ''Evermore'', ''[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]'' found Swift exploring "exceedingly complex human emotions with precision and devastation".<ref>{{Cite web|last=Olivier|first=Bobby|date=December 11, 2020|title=Taylor Swift's 'Evermore' Is an Undeniable Folk-Pop Masterpiece|url=https://www.spin.com/2020/12/taylor-swift-evermore-album-review/|access-date=February 1, 2021|work=[[Spin (magazine)|Spin]]}}</ref> ''Consequence'' stated her 2020 albums "offered a chance for doubters to see Swift's songwriting power on full display, but the truth is that her pen has always been her sword" and that her writing prowess took "different forms" as she transformed from "teenage wunderkind to a confident and careful adult."<ref name=":21" />

Swift's [[Bridge (music)|bridges]] have been underscored as one of the best aspects of her songs<ref>{{Cite web|last=Murphy|first=Sam|date=2021-11-10|title=How 'Red' Became The Most Pivotal Record In Taylor Swift's Career|url=https://junkee.com/taylor-swift-red-importance/314415|access-date=2021-11-10|website=[[Junkee]]|language=en-US}}</ref><ref name=":21" /> and earned her the title "Queen of Bridges" from media outlets.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Nguyen|first=Stacey|date=2021-07-12|title=Here's a Breakdown of Taylor Swift's "All Too Well" Before We Get the 10-Minute Version|url=https://www.popsugar.com/node/48404491|access-date=2021-11-10|website=[[PopSugar]]|language=en-US}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine|last=Bruner|first=Raisa|date=May 24, 2021|title=How Olivia Rodrigo Become America's Biggest New Pop Star|url=https://time.com/6050587/olivia-rodrigo-sour/|access-date=2021-11-10|magazine=[[Time (magazine)|Time]]|language=en}}</ref> Awarding Swift with the Songwriter Icon Award in 2021, the [[National Music Publishers' Association]] remarked that "no one is more influential when it comes to writing music today" than her.<ref>{{Cite web|date=May 24, 2021|title=NMPA to Honor Taylor Swift with Songwriter Icon Award Among Other 2021 Annual Meeting Honorees|url=https://www.nmpa.org/nmpa-to-honor-taylor-swift-with-songwriter-icon-award-among-other-2021-annual-meeting-honorees/|access-date=May 24, 2021|website=[[National Music Publishers' Association]]}}</ref> ''[[The Week]]'' deemed Swift the foremost female songwriter of modern times.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Linker|first=Damon|date=November 26, 2021|title=Taylor Swift, Phoebe Bridgers, and Rihanna: How women took over songwriting|url=https://theweek.com/feature/1007434/how-women-took-over-the-top-ranks-of-the-songwriting-pantheon|access-date=2021-11-28|website=The Week|language=en}}</ref>

=== Music videos ===
Swift has collaborated with many different directors to produce her music videos, and over time she has become more involved with writing and directing. She has her own production house, Taylor Swift Productions, Inc., which is credited with producing music videos for singles such as "Me!",<ref>{{cite news |last1=Coscarelli |first1=Joe |title=Taylor Swift Releases 'Me!,' a New Song Featuring Brendon Urie |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2019/04/26/arts/music/taylor-swift-me.html |access-date=June 20, 2019 |work=[[The New York Times]] |date=April 26, 2019 |archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190515195039/https://www.nytimes.com/2019/04/26/arts/music/taylor-swift-me.html |archive-date=May 15, 2019 |url-status=live }}</ref> and is known for hiding elaborate clues and [[Easter egg (media)|easter eggs]] in her work.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.seventeen.com/celebrity/music/a31135986/taylor-swift-the-man-music-video-easter-eggs/|title=Every Easter Egg in Taylor Swift's New Music Video "The Man": As always, there are a ton.|last=Twersky|first=Carolyn|website=Seventeen|date=February 27, 2020|access-date=May 13, 2020}}</ref> In 2010, Swift co-directed the music video for "Mine" with [[Roman White]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache:71z8LAzW7OkJ:www.mtv.com/news/2296264/video-taylor-swift-mine-2/+&cd=1&hl=en&ct=clnk&gl=us&client=safari|title=Video Premiere: Taylor Swift, 'Mine'|last=Anitai|first=Tamar|date=August 27, 2010|website=[[MTV News]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190429190835/http://webcache.googleusercontent.com/search?q=cache%3A71z8LAzW7OkJ%3Awww.mtv.com%2Fnews%2F2296264%2Fvideo-taylor-swift-mine-2%2F+&cd=1&hl=en&ct=clnk&gl=us&client=safari|archive-date=April 29, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> In 2011, she continued to collaborate with White on the music videos for "Mean" and "[[Ours (song)|Ours]]". Swift developed the concept and [[Film treatment|treatment]] for "Mean".<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1663245/taylor-swifts-mean-video-debuts-friday/|title=Taylor Swift's "Mean" Video Debuts Friday|last=cmt.com staff|date=May 4, 2011|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190619161133/http://www.cmt.com/news/1663245/taylor-swifts-mean-video-debuts-friday/|archive-date=June 19, 2019|url-status=live|access-date=June 19, 2019}}</ref> In an interview, White elaborated that Swift "was keenly involved in writing the treatment, casting and wardrobe. And she stayed for both the 15-hour shooting days, even when she wasn't in the scenes."<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.cmt.com/news/1663418/offstage-taylor-swift-isnt-mean-at-all-director-says/|title=OFFSTAGE: Taylor Swift Isn't "Mean" at All, Director Says|last=Bonaguro|first=Alison|date=May 6, 2011|publisher=[[CMT (U.S. TV channel)|CMT News]]|access-date=June 20, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190619161135/http://www.cmt.com/news/1663418/offstage-taylor-swift-isnt-mean-at-all-director-says/|archive-date=June 19, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> Swift wrote the concept for the "Ours" music video and then brought in White to direct, who described her vision of both videos as being "storylines".<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.taylorswift.com/news/53083|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20111202122439/http://www.taylorswift.com/news/53083|url-status=dead|archive-date=December 2, 2011|title=E! Online Will Debut "Ours" Music Video Fridaz December 2nd!|last=Swift|first=Taylor|date=November 29, 2011|publisher=taylorswift.com|access-date=June 20, 2019}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://tasteofcountry.com/taylor-swift-ours-video-behind-the-scenes-one/|title=Taylor Swift Gives Behind-the-Scenes Look at 'Ours' Video – Webisode One|last=Iasimone|first=Ashley|date=December 4, 2011|website=[[Taste of Country]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190619161135/https://tasteofcountry.com/taylor-swift-ours-video-behind-the-scenes-one/|archive-date=June 19, 2019|url-status=dead}}</ref>

From 2014 to 2018, Swift collaborated with director [[Joseph Kahn]] on eight music videos—four each from her albums ''1989'' and ''Reputation''. Kahn has praised Swift's involvement in the craft.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.etonline.com/exclusive-taylor-swifts-director-joseph-kahn-how-her-image-invokes-double-standard-shes-genius|title=Exclusive: Taylor Swift's Director Joseph Kahn on How Her Image Invokes a Double Standard: 'She's a Genius'|last=Tailor|first=Leena|date=September 1, 2017|website=etonline.com|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190619163600/https://www.etonline.com/exclusive-taylor-swifts-director-joseph-kahn-how-her-image-invokes-double-standard-shes-genius|archive-date=June 19, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> In 2014, Swift worked with [[American Express]] for her "Blank Space" music video (which Kahn directed), and released the interactive app ''AMEX Unstaged: Taylor Swift Experience''. Swift received starring and executive producer credit and won a [[Primetime Emmy Award]] for [[Primetime Emmy Award for Outstanding Interactive Program|Outstanding Interactive Program]] in 2015 for the app.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/taylor-swift-wins-emmy-interactive-821735|title=Taylor Swift and Jimmy Fallon Among Early Emmy Winners|last=O'Connell|first=Michael|date=October 9, 2015|website=[[The Hollywood Reporter]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190619164926/https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/news/taylor-swift-wins-emmy-interactive-821735|archive-date=June 19, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> She received producing credit in her music video for "Bad Blood" and won a [[Grammy Awards|Grammy Award]] for [[Best Music Video]] in 2016.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.thefashionspot.com/buzz-news/latest-news/590025-taylor-swifts-bad-blood-music-video/|title=Peep Taylor Swift's Star-Studded Cast for Her 'Bad Blood' Music Video|last=Forbes|first=Jihan|website=The Fashion Spot|date=May 14, 2015|access-date=May 13, 2020}}</ref> Swift developed the concept, wrote the treatment for, and starred in the music video for the Sugarland song "Babe" (2018).<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://people.com/country/taylor-swift-sugarland-babe-music-video/|title=Sugarland's Steamy 'Babe' Video Treatment Was Taylor Swift's Idea: 'She Reached Out to Us'|last=Kruh|first=Nancy|date=June 9, 2018|website=[[People (magazine)|People]]|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190502042938/https://people.com/country/taylor-swift-sugarland-babe-music-video/|archive-date=May 2, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> She has since emerged as a music video director herself, co-directing the music videos for three ''Lover'' singles: "Me!" with [[Dave Meyers (director)|Dave Meyers]], and "You Need to Calm Down" and "Lover" with Drew Kirsch.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-brendon-urie-me-826952/|title=Watch Taylor Swift, Brendon Urie's Colorful 'ME!' Video|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|last=Spanos|first=Brittany|date=April 25, 2019|access-date=April 25, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190426043044/https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-brendon-urie-me-826952/|archive-date=April 26, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.nme.com/news/music/taylor-swift-lover-colourful-video-2541024|title=Watch Taylor Swift's colourful new video for 'Lover'|last=Moore|first=Sam|website=[[NME]]|date=August 23, 2019|access-date=August 27, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190827182604/https://www.nme.com/news/music/taylor-swift-lover-colourful-video-2541024|archive-date=August 27, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> She co-executive produced the second of them with [[Todrick Hall]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/watch-taylor-swift-katy-perry-you-need-to-calm-down-video-848857/|title=Watch Taylor Swift Reunite With Katy Perry in 'You Need to Calm Down' Video|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|last=Zemler|first=Emily|date=June 17, 2019|access-date=June 17, 2019|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20190617123913/https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/watch-taylor-swift-katy-perry-you-need-to-calm-down-video-848857/|archive-date=June 17, 2019|url-status=live}}</ref> Swift was the sole director of the videos for "The Man", for which she won the [[MTV Video Music Award for Best Direction]] in 2020; "Cardigan"; and "Willow", for which Swift was nominated again for Best Direction at the 2021 Video Music Awards.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nme.com/blogs/every-incredible-easter-egg-in-taylor-swifts-the-man-video-2615495|title=Every incredible Easter Egg in Taylor Swift's 'The Man' video|last=Mylrea|first=Hannah|website=[[NME]]|date=February 28, 2020|access-date=March 9, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine|title=Taylor Swift Blends Fantastical With Personal in 'Cardigan' Video|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-news/taylor-swift-cardigan-video-folklore-1032977/|last1=Spanos|first1=Brittany|last2=Legaspi|first2=Althea|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=July 24, 2020|access-date=July 27, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite magazine|title=Justin Bieber & Megan Thee Stallion Lead 2021 MTV VMA Nominations|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/awards/9613274/2021-mtv-vma-nominations-list|access-date=2021-08-17|magazine=Billboard|language=en}}</ref>

== Public image ==

Continues|url=https://www.thecut.com/2013/06/taylor-swift-slut-shaming-continues.html|access-date=November 4, 2021|website=[[The Cut (website)|The Cut]]}}</ref> Swift has addressed these issues in her music. In "Blank Space", she [[Parody|parodies]] her portrayal by the media as "a girl who's crazy but seductive but glamorous but nuts but manipulative".<ref name="GQm">{{cite magazine|last=Klosterman|first=Chuck|date=October 15, 2015|title=Taylor Swift on 'Bad Blood,' Kanye West, and How People Interpret Her Lyrics|url=https://www.gq.com/story/taylor-swift-gq-cover-story|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20151018020927/http://www.gq.com/story/taylor-swift-gq-cover-story|archive-date=October 18, 2015|access-date=October 18, 2015|magazine=[[GQ]]}}</ref> Much of ''Reputation'' was conceived under the "intense" media scrutiny she experienced in 2015 and 2016,<ref name=":19" /> which caused her to adopt a dark, defensive [[alter ego]] on the album.<ref>{{cite web|last=Furdyk|first=Brent|date=September 27, 2019|title=Taylor Swift's 'Lover' Certified Platinum After Just 4 Weeks|url=https://etcanada.com/news/514258/taylor-swifts-lover-certified-platinum-after-just-4-weeks/|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200424231342/https://etcanada.com/news/514258/taylor-swifts-lover-certified-platinum-after-just-4-weeks/|archive-date=April 24, 2020|access-date=November 3, 2021|website=[[ET Canada]]}}</ref> She further criticized sexist double standards and [[gaslighting]] in her songs "[[The Man (Taylor Swift song)|The Man]]" (2019) and "[[Mad Woman]]" (2020), respectively.<ref>{{Cite web|last=July 24|first=Lauren Huff|date=July 24, 2020|title=Taylor Swift's 'Mad Woman' picks up where 'The Man' left off|url=https://ew.com/music/taylor-swift-mad-woman/|access-date=November 4, 2021|website=Entertainment Weekly|language=en}}</ref> When asked "why sing to the haters?" by [[CBS]] journalist [[Tracy Smith (journalist)|Tracy Smith]], Swift replied, "well, when they stop coming for me, I will stop singing to them".<ref>{{Cite web |last=Baumgartner |first=Scott |url=https://www.etonline.com/taylor-swift-on-her-haters-you-dont-have-to-forgive-and-you-dont-have-to-forget-131169 |title=Taylor Swift on Her Haters: 'You Don't Have to Forgive and You Don't Have to Forget'|access-date=November 4, 2021 |website=ET Online |date=August 29, 2019}}</ref>

== Impact ==
Swift's career helped shape the modern country music scene.<ref name="guardian country">{{cite web|url=https://www.theguardian.com/music/2014/mar/13/country-music-taylor-swift-nashville-radio-2|title=Detwanging country music: how Nashville took the UK|first=Colin|last=Crummy|work=[[The Guardian]]|date=March 13, 2014|access-date=September 23, 2021}}</ref> According to music journalist [[Jody Rosen]], Swift is the first country artist whose fame reached the world beyond the U.S.<ref name="Rosen" /> Her chart success extended to Asia and the U.K., where country music had previously not been popular.<ref name="guardian country"/><ref name="Rosen"/> Following Swift's rise to fame, country labels became more interested in signing young singers who write their own music.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/news/6386008/how-billboard-woman-of-the-year-taylor-swift-changed-country-music|title=4 Ways Billboard Woman of the Year Taylor Swift Changed Country Music|last=Tannembaum|first=Rob|date=September 12, 2014|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=December 31, 2019}}</ref> With her autobiographical narratives revolving around romance and heartbreak,<ref name="Rosen">{{cite web|url=https://www.vulture.com/2013/11/taylor-swift-reigning-queen-of-pop.html|title=Why Taylor Swift Is the Reigning Queen of Pop|first=Jody|last=Rosen|work=[[New York (magazine)|New York]]|date=November 17, 2013|access-date=November 9, 2020}}</ref> Swift introduced the genre to a younger generation that could relate to her personally.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/7430895/taylor-swift-music-career-ten-years-impact-country|title=Love Story: The Impact of Taylor Swift's First Decade in Music|last=Roland|first=Tom|date=July 7, 2016|magazine=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=December 31, 2019|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160714142858/https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/country/7430895/taylor-swift-music-career-ten-years-impact-country|archive-date=July 14, 2016}}</ref> Critics have since noted the impact of her sound on various albums released by female country singers such as [[Kacey Musgraves]],<ref>{{Cite web|last=Wilson|first=Carl|date=March 3, 2018|title=Taylor Swift Left a Blank Space in Country Music. Now Kacey Musgraves Could Fill It.|url=https://slate.com/culture/2018/03/kacey-musgraves-and-ashley-mcbrydes-new-albums-reviewed.html|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210304204538/https://slate.com/culture/2018/03/kacey-musgraves-and-ashley-mcbrydes-new-albums-reviewed.html|archive-date=March 4, 2021|access-date=August 24, 2021|website=Slate Magazine}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Hodgkinson|first=Will|date=March 30, 2018|title=Pop review: Kacey Musgraves: Golden Hour|work=[[The Times]]|url=https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/pop-review-kacey-musgraves-golden-hour-qvbl82lsz|url-status=live|url-access=subscription|access-date=August 24, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20201031165918/https://www.thetimes.co.uk/article/pop-review-kacey-musgraves-golden-hour-qvbl82lsz|archive-date=October 31, 2020}}</ref> [[Maren Morris]],<ref>{{Cite web|last=St. Asaph|first=Katherine|date=March 9, 2019|title=Maren Morris: Girl|url=https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/maren-morris-girl/|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210317231400/https://pitchfork.com/reviews/albums/maren-morris-girl/|archive-date=March 17, 2021|access-date=August 24, 2021|website=Pitchfork}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Willman|first=Chris|date=March 7, 2019|title=Album Review: Maren Morris' Girl|url=https://variety.com/2019/music/news/maren-morris-girl-album-review-1203157512/|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210411030724/https://variety.com/2019/music/news/maren-morris-girl-album-review-1203157512/|archive-date=April 11, 2021|access-date=August 24, 2021|website=Variety}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Johnson|first=Ellen|date=March 8, 2019|title=Maren Morris: GIRL Review|url=https://www.pastemagazine.com/music/maren-morris/maren-morris-girl-review/|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210723141551/https://www.pastemagazine.com/music/maren-morris/maren-morris-girl-review/|archive-date=July 23, 2021|access-date=August 24, 2021|website=Paste}}</ref> and [[Kelsea Ballerini]].<ref>{{Cite news|last=Zoladz|first=Lindsay|date=September 11, 2020|title=Kelsea Ballerini, Both Sides Now|work=The New York Times|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/09/11/arts/music/kelsea-ballerini-review.html|url-status=live|url-access=limited|access-date=August 24, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200914135413/https://www.nytimes.com/2020/09/11/arts/music/kelsea-ballerini-review.html|archive-date=September 14, 2020}}</ref> ''[[Rolling Stone]]'' listed Swift's country music as one of the biggest influences on 2010s pop music<ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Martoccio|first1=Angie|last2=Spanos|first2=Brittany|last3=Blistein|first3=Jon|last4=Bernstein|first4=Jonathan|last5=Shaffer|first5=Claire|date=December 23, 2019|title=The Biggest Influences on Pop in the 2010s|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/biggest-pop-influences-on-2010s-927808/|access-date=December 25, 2020|magazine=[[Rolling Stone]]}}</ref> and ranked her 80th in their list of 100 Greatest Country Artists of All Time.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-lists/100-greatest-country-artists-of-all-time-195775/carrie-underwood-19-195842/|title=100 Greatest Country Artists of All Time|date=June 15, 2017|work=Rolling Stone|access-date=April 4, 2021}}</ref>[[File:Phoenix-Musical Intrument Museum-Taylo Swift Les Pual guitar.jpg|upright|thumb|right|alt=A photograph of Swift's decorated red Les Paul guitar and cordless microphone|Swift's [[Gibson Les Paul|Les Paul]] guitar and microphone in the [[Musical Instrument Museum (Phoenix)|Musical Instrument Museum of Phoenix]]]]Her onstage performance with guitars contributed to the "Taylor Swift factor", a phenomenon to which the rise in guitar sales to women, a previously ignored demographic, is attributed.<ref>{{cite web |last1=O'Connor |first1=Roisin |title=Half of all new guitar players are women, finds study |url=https://www.independent.co.uk/arts-entertainment/music/news/new-guitar-players-women-men-gender-split-fender-taylor-swift-a8589786.html |website=[[The Independent]] |access-date=October 20, 2020 |date=October 18, 2018}}</ref><ref>{{cite magazine |last1=Wang |first1=Amy X. |title=Guitars Are Getting More Popular. So Why Do We Think They're Dying? |url=https://www.rollingstone.com/pro/news/guitars-are-getting-more-popular-so-why-do-we-think-theyre-dying-630446/ |magazine=[[Rolling Stone]] |access-date=October 20, 2020 |date=May 22, 2018}}</ref> ''[[Pitchfork (website)|Pitchfork]]'' opined that Swift changed the contemporary music landscape forever with her "unprecedented path from teenage country prodigy to global pop sensation" and a "singularly perceptive" discography that consistently accommodates both musical and cultural shifts.<ref>{{Cite web|date=October 4, 2021|title=The 200 Most Important Artists of Pitchfork's First 25 Years|url=https://pitchfork.com/features/lists-and-guides/most-important-artists/|access-date=October 4, 2021|website=[[Pitchfork (website)|Pitchfork]]}}</ref> ''[[Clash (magazine)|Clash]]'' stated that Swift's genre-spanning career encouraged her peers to experiment with various genres.<ref name=":23" /> Music journalist Nick Catucci wrote that, in being personal and vulnerable in her lyrics, Swift helped make space for later pop stars like [[Billie Eilish]], [[Ariana Grande]], and [[Halsey (singer)|Halsey]] to do the same.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last1=Catucci|first1=Nick|date=2019-08-23|title=Taylor Swift Reaches For New Heights of Personal and Musical Liberation on 'Lover'|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/music/music-album-reviews/taylor-swift-lover-875442/|access-date=2021-08-18|magazine=Rolling Stone|language=en-US}}</ref> According to ''[[The Guardian]]'', Swift leads the rebirth of [[poptimism]] in the 21st-century with her ambitious artistic vision.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Gormely|first=Ian|date=December 3, 2014|title=Taylor Swift leads poptimism's rebirth|url=http://www.theguardian.com/music/2014/dec/03/taylor-swift-poptimism|access-date=August 2, 2021|website=The Guardian|language=en}}</ref>

Publications consider Swift's million-selling albums an anomaly in the [[media streaming|streaming]]-dominated music industry following the decline of the [[album era]] in the 2010s.<ref name="bloomberg" /><ref name="nymag10s" /> For this reason, [[musicologists]] Mary Fogarty and Gina Arnold regard her "the last great rock star".<ref>{{Cite journal|last1=Fogarty|first1=Mary|last2=Arnold|first2=Gina|date=October 1, 2021|title=Are You Ready for It? Re-Evaluating Taylor Swift|url=https://doi.org/10.1080/07494467.2021.1976586|journal=Contemporary Music Review|volume=40|issue=1|pages=1–10|doi=10.1080/07494467.2021.1976586|s2cid=238241276|issn=0749-4467|access-date=October 3, 2021|via=[[Taylor & Francis]]}}</ref> Swift is the only artist to have [[Lists of fastest-selling albums#United States|four albums sell over one million copies]] in one week since [[Nielsen SoundScan]] began tracking sales for the ''Billboard'' 200 in 1991.<ref name="bloomberg">{{cite news|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20160313072511/https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2014-11-12/taylor-swift-and-big-machine-are-the-music-industry|url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2014-11-12/taylor-swift-and-big-machine-are-the-music-industry|title=Taylor Swift Is the Music Industry|first=Devin|last=Leonard|website=[[Bloomberg News]]|date=November 12, 2014|url-status=live|access-date=August 11, 2020|archive-date=March 13, 2016|url-access=subscription}}</ref> To ''New York'' magazine, her million sales figures prove that she is "the one bending the music industry to her will".<ref name="nymag10s">{{cite web|url=https://www.vulture.com/2019/12/taylor-swift-in-the-2010s.html|title=What Were the 2010s?|first=Lindsay|last=Zoladz|work=[[New York (magazine)|New York]]|date=December 30, 2019|access-date=November 22, 2020}}</ref> Swift also contributed to the [[vinyl revival|resurgence of vinyl sales]] in the 21st century.<ref>{{Cite magazine|last=DiGiacomo|first=Frank|date=June 8, 2021|title=Hip-Hop, R&B And Pop Challenge Rock's Vinyl Dominance In 2021|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/deep-dive/how-vinyl-got-its-groove-back/9584127/vinyl-albums-sales-genre-leaders-data|access-date=2021-07-16|magazine=Billboard|url-access=subscription}}</ref>

Swift has been recognized for challenging music industry norms.<ref name=":14">{{Cite web|last=Khan|first=Fawzia|date=June 18, 2021|title=The Might Of Taylor Swift|url=https://elle.in/article/the-might-of-taylor-swift/|access-date=October 20, 2021|website=[[Elle (magazine)|Elle]]|language=en-US}}</ref> Her actions have fostered debate over reforms to [[Comparison of on-demand music streaming services|on-demand music streaming]] and prompted awareness of [[intellectual property]] rights among younger musicians.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.musicweek.com/interviews/read/i-come-with-opinions-about-how-we-can-better-our-industry-taylor-swift-the-music-week-interview/077961|title='I come with opinions about how we can better our industry': Taylor Swift|last=Sutherland|first=Mark|magazine=[[Music Week]]|date=December 13, 2019|access-date=April 27, 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.nytimes.com/2014/11/06/arts/music/sales-of-taylor-swifts-1989-intensify-streaming-debate.html|title=Sales of Taylor Swift's '1989' Intensify Streaming Debate|first=Ben|last=Sisario|date=November 6, 2014|work=[[The New York Times]]|access-date=August 11, 2020}}</ref><ref name="Smith">{{cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/entertainment-arts-33222489|title=Five ways Taylor Swift is changing the world|last=Smith|first=Neil|date=June 22, 2015|access-date=December 31, 2019|website=[[BBC]]}}</ref> According to ''Rolling Stone'', her opposition to low royalties for artists from streaming services such as [[Spotify]] and [[Apple Music]], along with her efforts to claim ownership of her masters, were two of the music industry's most defining moments in the 2010s decade.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/pro/lists/the-50-most-important-music-moments-of-the-decade-912772/|title=The 50 Most Important Music Moments of the Decade|work=[[Rolling Stone]]|date=November 25, 2019|access-date=October 10, 2020}}</ref> [[Evening Standard|''The Standard'']] said Swift is "one of few artists with the power and profile to create change in the music world", and hence her decision to re-record her back catalog "motivates less established musicians to fight for better record deals."<ref>{{Cite news|last=Rosseinsky|first=Katie|date=October 29, 2021|title=How Taylor Swift is changing the music industry a re-record at a time|newspaper=[[Evening Standard]]|url=https://www.standard.co.uk/insider/taylor-swift-rerecording-albums-masters-fearless-b928211.html|url-status=live|access-date=April 23, 2021|archive-date=April 9, 2021|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20210409085520/https://www.standard.co.uk/insider/taylor-swift-rerecording-albums-masters-fearless-b928211.html}}</ref>

She was named [[Billboard Women in Music#Woman of the Decade Award|Woman of the Decade]] for the 2010s by ''Billboard'',<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/pop/8543996/taylor-swift-first-ever-woman-of-the-decade-award|title=Taylor Swift Will Receive First-Ever Woman of the Decade Honor at Billboard's Women in Music|date=November 18, 2019|work=[[Billboard (magazine)|Billboard]]|access-date=December 31, 2019}}</ref> became the first woman to earn the title [[American Music Awards#Artist of the Decade|Artist of the Decade]] (2010s) at the American Music Awards,<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.teenvogue.com/story/taylor-swift-artist-decade-amas-2019|title=Taylor Swift Is Named Artist of the Decade at AMAs 2019|last=Elizabeth|first=De|date=November 24, 2019|magazine=[[Teen Vogue]]|access-date=December 31, 2019}}</ref> and received the [[Brit Awards|Brit]] [[Brit Award for Outstanding Contribution to Music|Global Icon Award]] "in recognition of her immense impact on music across the world".<ref name=":6" /> Swift has been cited as an inspiration by various mainstream and indie recording artists, including [[Gracie Abrams]],<ref>{{Cite web|last=Blanchet|first=Brenton|date=2021-11-12|title=Gracie Abrams Is Already on to Her Next Moment of Strength|url=https://www.teenvogue.com/story/gracie-abrams-taylor-swift-strength-new-project-this-is-what-it-feels-like|access-date=2021-11-18|website=Teen Vogue|language=en-US}}</ref> [[Ruth B.]],<ref>{{Cite web|url=http://www.idolator.com/7616107/popping-up-ruth-b|title=Popping Up: Ruth B|date=November 25, 2015|access-date=June 25, 2020|website=[[Idolator (website)|Idolator]]|last = Wass|first = Mike}}</ref> [[Shamir Bailey]],<ref>{{Cite web|last=Curto|first=Justin|date=October 6, 2020|title=Taylor Swift, Canadian Singer-Songwriters, and More Influences on amassed over 114&nbsp;million units in global album consumption, including 78&nbsp;billion streams, as of May 2021.<ref name=":12">{{Cite web|date=May 9, 2021|title=Taylor Swift to receive BRITs Greatest of All Time Artists Chart.<ref>{{cite magazine|url=https://www.billboard.com/charts/greatest-of-all-time-artists|title=Greatest of All Time Artists|magazine=[[Billboard weeks (55) atop the [[Billboard 200|''Billboard'' 200]],<ref name="evermore">{{cite most number ones (23) on the ''Billboard'' [[Digital Songs]] chart.<ref>{{Cite magazine|date=February 23, 2021|title=Taylor Swift's 'Love Story (Taylor's Version)' Debuts at No. 1 on Hot Country Songs Chart: 'I'm So Grateful to the Fans'|url=https://www.billboard.com/articles/business/chart-beat/9529564/taylor-swift-love-story-number-one-hot-country-songs/|access-date=February 23, Swift became the first female artist to have five albums chart for 150 weeks each on the ''Billboard'' 200 with ''1989'', ''Taylor Swift'', ''Fearless'', ''Red'' and ''Reputation''.<ref>{{Cite web|date=2021-08-03|title=Taylor Swift's Latest Chart Feat Shows Off Her Career-Long She has the most number-one albums in the United Kingdom and Ireland for a female artist in this millennium<ref>{{Cite web|date=July 31, 2020|title=Taylor Swift's Folklore debuts at UK Albums Number 1|url=https://www.officialcharts.com/chart-news/taylor-swift-s-folklore-debuts-at-number-1-on-the-official-albums-chart__30661/|access-date=February 23, 2021|website=Official Charts}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=November 5, 2020|title=Female artists with the most Irish Number 1 albums since Charts}}</ref> and is the best-selling artist of all time on Chinese digital music platforms, earning {{Currency|159,000,000|RMB}} from her discography.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Wang|first=Dennis|date=April 16, 2021|title=Taylor Swift's Fearless hits the right note in China, again|url=http://en.people.cn/n3/2021/0416/c90000-9840061.html|access-date=June 26, 2021|website=[[People's Daily]]}}</ref> Swift is the second highest-certified female digital singles artist (and third overall) in the U.S., with 134&nbsp;million total units certified by the [[Recording Industry Association of America]] (RIAA),<ref>{{cite web|title=RIAA – Top Artists (Digital Singles)|url=https://www.riaa.com/gold-platinum/?tab_active=top_tallies&ttt=TAS#search_section|access-date=October 27, 2020|website=[[Recording Industry Association of America]]}}</ref> and the first female artist to have both an album (''Fearless'') and a song ("Shake It Off") certified [[RIAA certification|Diamond]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.msn.com/en-au/entertainment/entertainmentmusic/there-are-only-34-songs-in-history-that-have-been-certified-diamond-%E2%80%94-here-they-all-are/ss-BB11dNwX|title=There are only 34 songs in history that have been certified diamond — here they all are|first=Callie|last=Ahlgrim|work=[[MSN]]|date=March 14, 2020|access-date=October 22, 2020}}</ref> She broke the record for the highest-grossing North American tour of all time with her [[Reputation Stadium Tour]] (2018)<ref>{{Cite magazine|date=November 30, 2018|title=Taylor Swift's Reputation Stadium Tour Breaks Record for Highest-Grossing U.S. Tour|url=http://www.billboard.com/articles/columns/chart-beat/8487606/taylor-swift-reputation-stadium-tour-breaks-record-highest-grossing-us-tour|access-date=June 29, 2020|magazine=Billboard}}</ref> and is the world's highest-grossing female touring act of the 2010s.<ref>{{Cite web|last=Aswad|first=Jem|date=November 22, 2019|title=U2 Tops Rolling Stones, Ed Sheeran as Highest-Grossing Touring Artist of the Decade|url=https://variety.com/2019/biz/news/u2-tops-rolling-stones-ed-sheeran-as-highest-grossing-touring-artist-of-the-decade-1203413348/|access-date=June == Other activities ==
=== Wealth and properties ===
In 2021, ''Forbes'' estimated Swift's net worth at US$550&nbsp;million,<ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.forbes.com/profile/taylor-swift/|title=America's Self Made Women|date=August 5, 2021|magazine=[[Forbes]]|access-date=August 5, 2021}}</ref> coming from her music, streaming royalties, merchandise, promotions, and tours.<ref name="Real Estate">Sources on Swift's real estate
